Data Science Roadmap
 A structured guide to entering and excelling in the data-driven world
Introduction
Data science sits at the intersection of mathematics, statistics, programming, and domain expertise. In 2026, it
remains one of the most in-demand career paths globally, powering decisions across healthcare, finance,
e-commerce, and beyond. This roadmap provides a structured, professional path from zero to job-ready data
scientist.
The field demands more than just coding ability. A strong dat
---
from zero to job-ready data
scientist.
The field demands more than just coding ability. A strong data scientist must communicate insights clearly,
understand business context, and apply rigorous statistical thinking. Learners should expect a rewarding but
demanding journey of approximately 10 to 14 months before reaching professional readiness.
Phase 1 — Mathematics and Statistics Foundations
Before writing a single line of Python, a learner must build a solid mathematical base. This phase typic
---
re writing a single line of Python, a learner must build a solid mathematical base. This phase typically requires
4 to 6 weeks of focused study.
 Linear Algebra: Vectors, matrices, matrix multiplication, eigenvalues, and eigenvectors form the backbone of
machine learning models.
 Calculus: Derivatives and gradients are essential for understanding how models learn through optimization.
 Probability and Statistics: Distributions, hypothesis testing, confidence intervals, and Bayesian thinking a
---
ity and Statistics: Distributions, hypothesis testing, confidence intervals, and Bayesian thinking are
non-negotiable.
 Recommended resources: Khan Academy for calculus and linear algebra; StatQuest for intuitive statistical
explanations.
Do not rush this phase. A weak mathematical foundation leads to surface-level understanding of algorithms,
limiting long-term career growth.
Phase 2 — Programming with Python
Python is the dominant language of data science. Learners should target 4 to 6 weeks
---
ng with Python
Python is the dominant language of data science. Learners should target 4 to 6 weeks to reach intermediate
Python proficiency.
 Core Python: Variables, data types, loops, functions, object-oriented programming, and file handling.
 NumPy: Efficient array operations and numerical computing, the foundation of scientific Python.
 Pandas: Data manipulation, cleaning, grouping, merging, and aggregation — the most-used library in
day-to-day data work.
 Matplotlib and Seaborn: Visuali
---
, and aggregation — the most-used library in
day-to-day data work.
 Matplotlib and Seaborn: Visualization libraries for exploratory data analysis and result communication.
Practice on real datasets from Kaggle or UCI Machine Learning Repository. The goal is comfort, not perfection,
before moving forward.

Phase 3 — Machine Learning
Machine learning is the technical core of data science. Dedicate 8 to 10 weeks to this phase, using Scikit-learn as
the primary toolkit.
 Supervised Learning: Linea
---
8 to 10 weeks to this phase, using Scikit-learn as
the primary toolkit.
 Supervised Learning: Linear regression, logistic regression, decision trees, random forests, support vector
machines, and gradient boosting.
 Unsupervised Learning: K-means clustering, hierarchical clustering, and dimensionality reduction with PCA.
 Model Evaluation: Cross-validation, confusion matrices, ROC-AUC, precision-recall, and hyperparameter
tuning.
 Feature Engineering: Encoding, scaling, imputation, and select
---
-recall, and hyperparameter
tuning.
 Feature Engineering: Encoding, scaling, imputation, and selection — often more impactful than algorithm
choice.
Each algorithm should be understood both mathematically and practically. Implement models from scratch at least
once before relying entirely on library calls.
Phase 4 — Deep Learning and Specialized Domains
After mastering classical machine learning, expand into deep learning and one or two specialized areas. Allow 6
to 8 weeks.
 Neural Networks:
---
expand into deep learning and one or two specialized areas. Allow 6
to 8 weeks.
 Neural Networks: Feedforward networks, activation functions, backpropagation, and optimizers.
 Frameworks: TensorFlow and PyTorch are both industry-standard. PyTorch dominates research; TensorFlow
is widely used in production.
 Natural Language Processing: Text preprocessing, embeddings, transformer models, and large language
model fine-tuning.
 Computer Vision: CNNs, image classification, object detection, and
---
rge language
model fine-tuning.
 Computer Vision: CNNs, image classification, object detection, and transfer learning with pretrained models.
Tools, Databases, and Deployment
Modern data scientists must operate beyond Jupyter notebooks. Understanding data pipelines and deployment is
increasingly expected.
 SQL: Querying relational databases is essential. Master SELECT, JOIN, GROUP BY, subqueries, and
window functions.
 Cloud Platforms: AWS SageMaker, Google Vertex AI, or Azure ML for model tr
---
, and
window functions.
 Cloud Platforms: AWS SageMaker, Google Vertex AI, or Azure ML for model training and deployment at
scale.
 MLflow and DVC: Experiment tracking and data versioning for reproducible workflows.
 Docker: Containerization for consistent model serving environments.

Portfolio and Career Preparation
A portfolio of 3 to 5 well-documented projects is the most effective job application tool. Projects should
demonstrate the full workflow: data collection, cleaning, exploration,
---
cation tool. Projects should
demonstrate the full workflow: data collection, cleaning, exploration, modeling, evaluation, and communication.
 End-to-End Projects: Kaggle competitions, personal datasets, or real-world problems from your domain of
interest.
 GitHub: Maintain clean repositories with README files, notebooks, and reproducible code.
 Technical Writing: Blog posts explaining your methodology demonstrate communication skills highly valued
by employers.

DevOps and Cloud Engineering Roadmap
 From infrastructure fundamentals to production-grade cloud deployments
Introduction
DevOps is the practice of bridging software development and IT
---
-grade cloud deployments
Introduction
DevOps is the practice of bridging software development and IT operations to enable faster, more reliable
software delivery. In 2026, cloud-native DevOps engineering is among the highest-compensated technical
disciplines, driven by the universal adoption of cloud infrastructure across industries.
This roadmap covers Linux fundamentals, networking, containerization, CI/CD pipelines, infrastructure as code,
and cloud platforms. Expect a professional-readiness
---
tion, CI/CD pipelines, infrastructure as code,
and cloud platforms. Expect a professional-readiness timeline of 10 to 14 months with dedicated daily practice.
Phase 1 — Linux and Networking Fundamentals
The operating system is the foundation of all infrastructure work. Spend 4 to 6 weeks here.
 Linux CLI: File system navigation, permissions, process management, cron jobs, and shell scripting.
 Bash Scripting: Automate repetitive tasks, write deployment scripts, and manipulate files programmati
---
ash Scripting: Automate repetitive tasks, write deployment scripts, and manipulate files programmatically.
 Networking Basics: TCP/IP model, DNS, HTTP/HTTPS, firewalls, load balancers, and SSH.
 Recommended practice: Set up a local Linux VM using VirtualBox or WSL on Windows.
Phase 2 — Version Control and CI/CD
Modern software delivery depends on automated pipelines. This phase requires 4 to 5 weeks.
 Git: Branching strategies, merge conflicts, rebasing, and GitFlow workflow.
 GitHub Actions
---
eeks.
 Git: Branching strategies, merge conflicts, rebasing, and GitFlow workflow.
 GitHub Actions or GitLab CI: Define pipelines as code for automated testing and deployment.
 Jenkins: Widely used in enterprise environments; understanding pipeline-as-code with Jenkinsfile is valuable.
 Artifact Management: Tools like Nexus or JFrog Artifactory for managing build artifacts.

Phase 3 — Containers and Orchestration
Containerization has transformed software deployment. Devote 6 to 8 weeks to ma
---
rs and Orchestration
Containerization has transformed software deployment. Devote 6 to 8 weeks to mastering Docker and
Kubernetes.
 Docker: Images, containers, Dockerfiles, volumes, networks, and Docker Compose for multi-service setups.
 Kubernetes: Pods, deployments, services, ingress controllers, ConfigMaps, secrets, and Helm charts.
 Container Security: Image scanning, least-privilege containers, and runtime security tools like Falco.
 Service Mesh: Istio or Linkerd for advanced traffic m
---
ners, and runtime security tools like Falco.
 Service Mesh: Istio or Linkerd for advanced traffic management and observability in microservice
architectures.
Phase 4 — Infrastructure as Code
Manual infrastructure management does not scale. IaC tools bring consistency, repeatability, and version control
to infrastructure.
 Terraform: The industry-standard IaC tool for provisioning cloud resources across AWS, Azure, and GCP.
 Ansible: Agentless configuration management for automating software i
---
across AWS, Azure, and GCP.
 Ansible: Agentless configuration management for automating software installation and system configuration.
 Pulumi: Emerging IaC tool using general-purpose programming languages like Python and TypeScript.
 State Management: Remote backends like S3 with DynamoDB locking for team collaboration on Terraform
state.
Phase 5 — Cloud Platforms
Deep expertise in at least one major cloud provider is essential. AWS holds the largest market share and is the
recommended sta
---
one major cloud provider is essential. AWS holds the largest market share and is the
recommended starting point.
 AWS Core Services: EC2, S3, RDS, Lambda, VPC, IAM, CloudWatch, ECS, and EKS.
 Certifications: AWS Solutions Architect Associate is the most recognized entry-level cloud credential.
 Multi-Cloud Awareness: Understanding GCP and Azure architectures is increasingly valued in enterprise
roles.

Phase 6 — Monitoring and Observability
Production systems require comprehensive monitoring.

roles.

Phase 6 — Monitoring and Observability
Production systems require comprehensive monitoring. Allocate 3 to 4 weeks to this critical discipline.
 Prometheus and Grafana: The standard open-source monitoring stack for metrics collection and
visualization.
 ELK Stack: Elasticsearch, Logstash, and Kibana for centralized log management and analysis.
 Distributed Tracing: Jaeger or Zipkin for tracing requests across microservices.
 Alerting: Define SLOs, SLAs, and error budgets; configure i
---
tracing requests across microservices.
 Alerting: Define SLOs, SLAs, and error budgets; configure intelligent alerting to avoid alert fatigue.

Cybersecurity Roadmap
 Building a career in ethical hacking, defense, and security engineering
Introduction
Cybersecurity is one of the fastest-growing fields in technology, with a global workforce shortage of millions of
professionals. Organizations of every size face daily threats from ransomware, phishing, supply chain attacks, and
advanced persistent threats. This creates exceptional
---
nsomware, phishing, supply chain attacks, and
advanced persistent threats. This creates exceptional career opportunities for trained security professionals.
This roadmap covers the full spectrum of cybersecurity: from foundational networking knowledge to penetration
testing, defensive operations, and cloud security. A disciplined learner can reach entry-level readiness in 10 to 12
months.
Phase 1 — Networking and OS Fundamentals
Security professionals must deeply understand what they are defendi
---
— Networking and OS Fundamentals
Security professionals must deeply understand what they are defending. Invest 4 to 6 weeks building this
foundation.
 Networking: OSI model, TCP/IP, DNS, DHCP, HTTP, HTTPS, TLS, VPNs, and firewalls.
 Linux: Command-line proficiency, file permissions, process management, and log analysis.
 Windows: Active Directory, Group Policy, Windows Event Logs, and PowerShell scripting.
 Virtualization: Build a home lab using VirtualBox or VMware with multiple VMs for pra
---
l scripting.
 Virtualization: Build a home lab using VirtualBox or VMware with multiple VMs for practice.
Phase 2 — Core Security Concepts
Understanding fundamental security principles is prerequisite to specialization.
 CIA Triad: Confidentiality, Integrity, and Availability as the core security framework.
 Cryptography: Symmetric and asymmetric encryption, hashing, PKI, certificates, and TLS handshake.
 Authentication and Authorization: MFA, OAuth 2.0, SAML, and zero-trust architecture.

---
handshake.
 Authentication and Authorization: MFA, OAuth 2.0, SAML, and zero-trust architecture.
 Vulnerability Management: CVE system, CVSS scoring, patch management, and risk prioritization.

Phase 3 — Offensive Security and Penetration Testing
Ethical hacking teaches security professionals to think like attackers. Spend 8 to 10 weeks on this phase.
 Reconnaissance: OSINT techniques, Shodan, Maltego, and passive information gathering.
 Scanning and Enumeration: Nmap, Nessus, Nikto, and ser
---
Maltego, and passive information gathering.
 Scanning and Enumeration: Nmap, Nessus, Nikto, and service fingerprinting.
 Exploitation: Metasploit Framework, manual exploitation, buffer overflows, and web app attacks.
 OWASP Top 10: SQL injection, XSS, CSRF, IDOR, SSRF, and broken authentication are must-know
vulnerabilities.
 Post-Exploitation: Privilege escalation, lateral movement, persistence, and data exfiltration techniques.
Phase 4 — Defensive Security and Blue Team
Defensive operation
---
ce, and data exfiltration techniques.
Phase 4 — Defensive Security and Blue Team
Defensive operations protect organizations from real-world attacks.
 SIEM: Splunk and Microsoft Sentinel for log aggregation, correlation, and alerting.
 Incident Response: Detection, containment, eradication, and recovery playbooks.
 Threat Hunting: Proactively searching for attackers who have evaded automated detection.
 Endpoint Detection and Response: CrowdStrike, SentinelOne, and Microsoft Defender for Endp
---
ection.
 Endpoint Detection and Response: CrowdStrike, SentinelOne, and Microsoft Defender for Endpoint.
Phase 5 — Specialized Tracks
After mastering the fundamentals, choose a specialization based on career goals.
 Cloud Security: AWS and Azure security services, IAM misconfiguration, and cloud-native threats.
 Application Security: SAST, DAST, code review, threat modeling, and DevSecOps integration.
 Digital Forensics: Memory analysis, disk forensics, and chain of custody procedures.
 Red
---
ration.
 Digital Forensics: Memory analysis, disk forensics, and chain of custody procedures.
 Red Team Operations: Advanced adversary simulation, C2 frameworks like Cobalt Strike and Havoc.

Machine Learning Engineering Roadmap
 Bridging research and production — building scalable ML systems
Introduction
Machine Learning Engineering (MLE) sits at the intersection of data science and software engineering. Unlike
data scientists who focus primarily on model development, ML engineers are responsible for the entire lifecycle:
data pipelines, model training infrastructure, deployment, monitor
---
onsible for the entire lifecycle:
data pipelines, model training infrastructure, deployment, monitoring, and scalability. In 2026, this role commands
among the highest salaries in the technology sector.
This roadmap targets individuals with some programming background who wish to build production-grade
machine learning systems. The expected timeline to professional readiness is 12 to 16 months.
Phase 1 — Software Engineering Fundamentals
Strong software engineering skills differentiate ML engine
---
ase 1 — Software Engineering Fundamentals
Strong software engineering skills differentiate ML engineers from data scientists. Spend 6 to 8 weeks solidifying
these foundations.
 Python Proficiency: Advanced Python including decorators, generators, context managers, type hints, and
async programming.
 Data Structures and Algorithms: Arrays, trees, graphs, sorting, and searching — essential for technical
interviews.
 System Design: Scalable architecture patterns, caching, message queues, and dis
---
hnical
interviews.
 System Design: Scalable architecture patterns, caching, message queues, and distributed system
fundamentals.
 Software Engineering Practices: Clean code, unit testing, code review, and continuous integration.
Phase 2 — Machine Learning Foundations
Build a rigorous understanding of core ML algorithms and evaluation methodologies. Allow 8 to 10 weeks.
 Supervised Learning: Regression, classification, ensemble methods, and gradient boosting with XGBoost
and LightGBM.
 Deep L
---
ression, classification, ensemble methods, and gradient boosting with XGBoost
and LightGBM.
 Deep Learning: Neural network architectures, CNNs, RNNs, LSTMs, transformers, and attention
mechanisms.
 MLOps Basics: Experiment tracking with MLflow, model versioning, and reproducible training pipelines.
 Feature Stores: Understanding Feast or Tecton for centralized feature management across teams.

Phase 3 — Data Engineering for ML
High-quality data pipelines are the foundation of reliable ML syst
---
Phase 3 — Data Engineering for ML
High-quality data pipelines are the foundation of reliable ML systems. This phase requires 6 to 8 weeks.
 Apache Spark: Distributed data processing for large-scale feature engineering and model training.
 Apache Kafka: Real-time data streaming for online feature computation and model serving.
 Airflow: Workflow orchestration for scheduling and monitoring data and training pipelines.
 Data Warehousing: Snowflake, BigQuery, and Delta Lake for analytical data s
---
nd training pipelines.
 Data Warehousing: Snowflake, BigQuery, and Delta Lake for analytical data storage at scale.
Phase 4 — Model Training Infrastructure
Production ML training differs significantly from notebook-based experimentation.
 Distributed Training: Horovod, DeepSpeed, and PyTorch DDP for training large models across GPU clusters.
 GPU Computing: CUDA basics, GPU memory management, and optimizing training throughput.
 Hyperparameter Optimization: Optuna, Ray Tune, and Bayesian opt
---
nd optimizing training throughput.
 Hyperparameter Optimization: Optuna, Ray Tune, and Bayesian optimization at scale.
 Cloud Training: AWS SageMaker, Google Vertex AI, and Azure ML for managed training infrastructure.
Phase 5 — Model Deployment and Serving
Getting models into production and serving them reliably is the core MLE challenge.
 Model Serving Frameworks: TorchServe, TensorFlow Serving, Triton Inference Server, and FastAPI
wrappers.
 Containerization: Docker and Kubernetes for sca
---
ng, Triton Inference Server, and FastAPI
wrappers.
 Containerization: Docker and Kubernetes for scalable, reproducible model serving environments.
 A/B Testing: Shadow deployment, canary releases, and statistical significance testing for model rollouts.
 Latency Optimization: Quantization, pruning, ONNX export, and batching strategies for low-latency inference.

Phase 6 — ML Monitoring and Reliability
Production ML systems degrade over time due to data and concept drift. Monitoring is essenti
---
ability
Production ML systems degrade over time due to data and concept drift. Monitoring is essential.
 Data Drift Detection: Evidently AI, Alibi Detect, and statistical tests for input distribution changes.
 Model Performance Monitoring: Tracking prediction accuracy, latency, and throughput in production.
 Retraining Pipelines: Automated triggers for model retraining when performance degrades below thresholds.
 Alerting: Integration with PagerDuty and Slack for real-time model health notif
---
below thresholds.
 Alerting: Integration with PagerDuty and Slack for real-time model health notifications.

UI/UX Design Roadmap
 Designing products that people love — from research to high-fidelity prototypes
Introduction
User Interfac
---
ing products that people love — from research to high-fidelity prototypes
Introduction
User Interface and User Experience design is the practice of creating digital products that are intuitive, accessible,
and visually compelling. In 2026, UX design has expanded beyond screens into voice interfaces, AR/VR
experiences, and AI-driven adaptive interfaces. Companies of every size invest heavily in design as a direct driver
of user retention and revenue.
This roadmap guides aspiring designers from fo
---
ign as a direct driver
of user retention and revenue.
This roadmap guides aspiring designers from foundational principles to a professional-grade portfolio. No prior
design experience is necessary, but attention to detail, empathy, and a critical eye are essential personal
qualities.
Phase 1 — Design Fundamentals
Before learning tools, internalize core design principles. Dedicate 3 to 4 weeks.
 Visual Design Principles: Balance, contrast, alignment, proximity, repetition, and hierarchy.
 Typog
---
isual Design Principles: Balance, contrast, alignment, proximity, repetition, and hierarchy.
 Typography: Font families, type scales, line height, kerning, and typographic hierarchy.
 Color Theory: Color models, palettes, accessibility contrast ratios (WCAG 2.1), and emotional associations.
 Grid Systems: 8-point grids, 12-column layouts, spacing systems, and responsive breakpoints.
Phase 2 — UX Research and Strategy
Design without research is guesswork. Spend 4 to 5 weeks learning research m
---
X Research and Strategy
Design without research is guesswork. Spend 4 to 5 weeks learning research methods.
 User Research Methods: Interviews, surveys, usability testing, card sorting, and diary studies.
 Personas and User Journey Maps: Synthesizing research into actionable design tools.
 Information Architecture: Sitemaps, navigation patterns, and content hierarchy.
 Competitive Analysis: Evaluating competitor products to identify opportunities and gaps.

Phase 3 — Wireframing and Prototyp
---
aluating competitor products to identify opportunities and gaps.

Phase 3 — Wireframing and Prototyping
Translate research into testable designs. Allow 4 to 6 weeks to build speed and confidence.
 Low-Fidelity Wireframes: Sketch or paper-based layouts to rapidly explore structural concepts.
 Mid-Fidelity Wireframes: Digital wireframes in Figma establishing layout, navigation, and content hierarchy.
 High-Fidelity Prototypes: Pixel-perfect interactive prototypes with transitions and micro-inte
---
hy.
 High-Fidelity Prototypes: Pixel-perfect interactive prototypes with transitions and micro-interactions.
 Prototyping Tools: Figma is the industry standard; Framer is preferred for advanced interactive prototypes.
Phase 4 — Figma Mastery
Figma proficiency is non-negotiable in 2026. Spend 4 to 6 weeks achieving professional-level Figma skills.
 Components and Auto Layout: Build reusable component libraries with variants and responsive auto layout.
 Design Tokens: Establish consistent colo
---
onent libraries with variants and responsive auto layout.
 Design Tokens: Establish consistent color, typography, and spacing tokens for scalable design systems.
 Dev Mode: Understand how developers inspect designs, extract specifications, and access assets.
 Plugins: FigJam for collaboration, Stark for accessibility checks, and Content Reel for realistic placeholder
data.
Phase 5 — Design Systems
Design systems enable consistent, scalable product development across large teams.
 Component L
---
ems
Design systems enable consistent, scalable product development across large teams.
 Component Libraries: Buttons, inputs, modals, navigation components, cards, and typography components.
 Documentation: Writing clear usage guidelines, do and dont examples, and accessibility notes.
 Handoff: Preparing assets for developer handoff with proper naming, spacing annotations, and asset exports.
 Reference Design Systems: Study Google Material Design 3, Apple Human Interface Guidelines, and IBM

Phase 6 — Accessibility and Inclusive Design
Accessible design is both an ethical responsibility and a legal requirement in many markets.
 WCAG 2.1 Guidelines: AA compliance for color contrast, keyboard navigation, and screen reader
compatibility.
 Accessible Components: Focus states, ARIA labels, skip navigation, and semantic structure.
 Inclusive Design Principles: Designing for dive
---
A labels, skip navigation, and semantic structure.
 Inclusive Design Principles: Designing for diverse abilities, languages, and cultural contexts.
 Testing Tools: axe DevTools, NVDA screen reader, and VoiceOver for accessibility validation.

Blockchain Development Roadmap
 Building decentralized applications and smart contracts on modern blockchain platforms
Introduction
Blockchain technology underpins decentralized finance, digital asset ownership, supply chain verification,
---
ain technology underpins decentralized finance, digital asset ownership, supply chain verification, and
identity management. In 2026, enterprise blockchain adoption continues to expand beyond cryptocurrency,
creating demand for skilled blockchain developers with strong software engineering foundations.
This roadmap assumes basic programming familiarity and covers blockchain fundamentals through professional
smart contract development and DApp deployment. The expected journey to professional comp
---
ofessional
smart contract development and DApp deployment. The expected journey to professional competence is 10 to 14
months.
Phase 1 — Blockchain Fundamentals
Technical understanding of blockchain architecture is prerequisite to development. Allow 3 to 4 weeks.
 Core Concepts: Distributed ledgers, consensus mechanisms, cryptographic hashing, and Merkle trees.
 Consensus Algorithms: Proof of Work, Proof of Stake, Delegated PoS, and practical Byzantine fault
tolerance.
 Public vs Private Bloc
---
rk, Proof of Stake, Delegated PoS, and practical Byzantine fault
tolerance.
 Public vs Private Blockchains: Ethereum, Bitcoin, Solana, and Hyperledger Fabric compared.
 Cryptography: Public-key cryptography, digital signatures, wallet addresses, and transaction verification.
Phase 2 — Ethereum and Smart Contracts
Ethereum remains the dominant smart contract platform. Spend 6 to 8 weeks here.
 Solidity: The primary smart contract language. Master data types, functions, modifiers, events, and
i
---
olidity: The primary smart contract language. Master data types, functions, modifiers, events, and
inheritance.
 EVM: Understanding the Ethereum Virtual Machine, gas mechanics, and transaction lifecycle.
 Development Frameworks: Hardhat is the recommended local development environment; Foundry is gaining
rapid adoption.
 OpenZeppelin: Industry-standard security-audited smart contract libraries for tokens, access control, and
upgradeable contracts.

Phase 3 — DeFi and Token Standards
Deep unde
---
for tokens, access control, and
upgradeable contracts.

Phase 3 — DeFi and Token Standards
Deep understanding of DeFi protocols accelerates professional contract development.
 ERC Standards: ERC-20 for fungible tokens, ERC-721 for NFTs, ERC-1155 for multi-tokens, and ERC-4337
for account abstraction.
 DeFi Protocols: Automated market makers, liquidity pools, lending protocols, and yield farming mechanics.
 Flash Loans: Understanding flash loan attacks and defensive patterns in smart contract
---
mechanics.
 Flash Loans: Understanding flash loan attacks and defensive patterns in smart contract design.
 MEV: Miner/validator extractable value, front-running, and sandwich attack awareness.
Phase 4 — Smart Contract Security
Security is the most critical discipline in blockchain development. Bugs result in permanent, irrecoverable loss of
funds.
 Common Vulnerabilities: Reentrancy, integer overflow, access control flaws, and oracle manipulation.
 Security Patterns: Checks-effects-interact

verflow, access control flaws, and oracle manipulation.

Introduction

---
velopment Roadmap
 Architecting robust, scalable server-side systems and APIs
Introduction
Backend development encompasses the server-side logic, databases, APIs, and infrastructure that power modern
applications. While users never see backend code directly, it determines the reliability, performance, and security
of every digital product. Backend engineers are among the most sought-after professionals across startups,
enterprises, and technology companies globally.
This roadmap follows a struct
---
onals across startups,
enterprises, and technology companies globally.
This roadmap follows a structured progression from core programming skills through system design and cloud
deployment. JavaScript with Node.js is used as the primary teaching language due to its ubiquity, but principles
transfer to Python, Go, Java, and other backend ecosystems.
Phase 1 — Programming Language Mastery
Choose one language and master it before exploring others. Allow 6 to 8 weeks.
 JavaScript / Node.js: Event l
---
language and master it before exploring others. Allow 6 to 8 weeks.
 JavaScript / Node.js: Event loop, asynchronous programming, promises, async/await, streams, and modules.
 Python: Equally valid choice, especially popular in data-adjacent backend roles. Flask and Django are the
primary frameworks.
 Go: Growing rapidly in infrastructure and high-performance API development due to its concurrency model.
 Java: Dominates enterprise backend development. Spring Boot is the industry-standard fr
---
ncy model.
 Java: Dominates enterprise backend development. Spring Boot is the industry-standard framework.
Phase 2 — APIs and Web Frameworks
Building APIs is the primary daily task of backend engineers. Spend 5 to 6 weeks.
 REST API Design: Resource naming, HTTP methods, status codes, pagination, filtering, and versioning.
 Express.js: Routing, middleware, error handling, and request/response lifecycle for Node.js APIs.
 GraphQL: Schema definition, resolvers, queries, mutations, and subscri
---
lifecycle for Node.js APIs.
 GraphQL: Schema definition, resolvers, queries, mutations, and subscriptions for flexible data APIs.
 API Security: JWT authentication, OAuth 2.0 flows, rate limiting, input validation, and HTTPS enforcement.

Phase 3 — Databases
Data persistence is the backbone of all backend systems. Allow 6 to 8 weeks.
 SQL: PostgreSQL is the recommended relational database. Master complex JOINs, window functions,
indexes, and transactions.
 ORMs: Prisma (Node.js) and SQLAlche
---
er complex JOINs, window functions,
indexes, and transactions.
 ORMs: Prisma (Node.js) and SQLAlchemy (Python) for productive database interactions with type safety.
 NoSQL: MongoDB for document storage, Redis for caching and session management, and Elasticsearch for
full-text search.
 Database Design: Normalization, entity-relationship diagrams, indexing strategies, and query optimization.
Phase 4 — System Design and Architecture
Senior backend engineers design systems, not just write code.
---
se 4 — System Design and Architecture
Senior backend engineers design systems, not just write code. Begin this phase after 4 to 5 months.
 Microservices: Service decomposition, inter-service communication with REST or gRPC, and service
discovery.
 Message Queues: RabbitMQ and Apache Kafka for asynchronous processing and event-driven
architectures.
 Caching Strategies: Cache-aside, write-through, and read-through patterns with Redis.
 API Gateway: Kong, AWS API Gateway, or Nginx for rate limi
---
, and read-through patterns with Redis.
 API Gateway: Kong, AWS API Gateway, or Nginx for rate limiting, authentication, and routing.

Production-ready code requires comprehensive testing discipline.
 Unit Testing: Jest (Node.js) or pytest (Python) for testing individual functions and modules.
 Integration Testing: Testing API endpoints with Supertest or Pytest-FastAPI.
 Test-Driven Development: Writing tests before implementation to improve design and catch
---
-FastAPI.
 Test-Driven Development: Writing tests before implementation to improve design and catch regressions.
 Code Quality: ESLint, Prettier, SonarQube, and pre-commit hooks for consistent, maintainable code.

Phase 6 — Deployment and Operations
Backend engineers must understand how their code runs in production.
 Docker: Containerizing Node.js and Python applications for consistent environments.
 CI/CD: GitHub Actions pipelines for automated testing, building, and deployment.

---
ments.
 CI/CD: GitHub Actions pipelines for automated testing, building, and deployment.
 Cloud Deployment: AWS EC2, Elastic Beanstalk, Lambda, or Render for application hosting.
 Logging and Monitoring: Winston/Pino for structured logging, Datadog or CloudWatch for observability.

Embedded Systems and IoT Roadmap
 Programming the physical world — microcontrollers, sensors, and connected devices
Introduction
Embedded systems are computing systems designed t
---
llers, sensors, and connected devices
Introduction
Embedded systems are computing systems designed to perform dedicated functions within larger mechanical or
electronic systems. From consumer electronics and industrial machinery to medical devices and smart home
technology, embedded software powers the physical world around us. The Internet of Things (IoT) extends this by
connecting embedded devices to cloud platforms for data collection and remote control.
This roadmap serves engineers, electro
---
es to cloud platforms for data collection and remote control.
This roadmap serves engineers, electronics enthusiasts, and computer science graduates seeking to enter the
embedded systems domain. Programming experience in any language is beneficial. The journey to professional
readiness spans 12 to 16 months.
Phase 1 — Electronics Fundamentals
Software alone is insufficient in embedded systems. Basic electronics knowledge is essential. Allow 4 to 5 weeks.
 Basic Electronics: Voltage, current, re
---
ic electronics knowledge is essential. Allow 4 to 5 weeks.
 Basic Electronics: Voltage, current, resistance, Ohm Law, capacitors, inductors, and transistors.
 Digital Logic: Binary, hexadecimal, logic gates, flip-flops, and Boolean algebra.
 Microcontroller Architecture: CPU, memory (Flash, RAM, EEPROM), peripherals, clock systems, and
interrupts.
 Tools: Multimeter, oscilloscope basics, breadboarding, and soldering — practical skills for hardware
debugging.
Phase 2 — C Programming for Embed
---
boarding, and soldering — practical skills for hardware
debugging.
Phase 2 — C Programming for Embedded Systems
C is the dominant language of embedded systems. Spend 6 to 8 weeks achieving embedded-grade C proficiency.
 Pointers and Memory: Pointer arithmetic, memory-mapped registers, and manual memory management.
 Bit Manipulation: Bitwise operators, masking, setting, clearing, and toggling individual bits in hardware
registers.
 Volatile Qualifier: Essential for hardware register access and
---
ividual bits in hardware
registers.
 Volatile Qualifier: Essential for hardware register access and interrupt service routine shared variables.
 Linker Scripts: Understanding how code is placed in Flash and how data sections are initialized in RAM.

Phase 3 — Microcontroller Programming
Apply C programming to real hardware. The STM32 series is recommended for professional-grade learning.
 STM32 with HAL/LL: Industry-standard ARM Cortex-M microcontrollers with excellent toolchain support.
 GP
---
with HAL/LL: Industry-standard ARM Cortex-M microcontrollers with excellent toolchain support.
 GPIO Control: Configuring input/output pins, LED control, button debouncing, and external interrupts.
 Communication Protocols: UART, SPI, I2C, and CAN bus — essential interfaces for sensors and peripherals.
 Timers and PWM: Timer configuration for precise timing, motor control, and LED dimming.
Phase 4 — Real-Time Operating Systems
Complex embedded applications require task scheduling and resourc
---
se 4 — Real-Time Operating Systems
Complex embedded applications require task scheduling and resource management. Allow 6 to 8 weeks.
 FreeRTOS: The most widely deployed RTOS in embedded systems. Tasks, queues, semaphores, and
mutexes.
 Task Design: Periodic tasks, event-driven tasks, and designing for deterministic response times.
 Interrupt Service Routines: Minimal ISR design, deferred processing via task notification and queues.
 RTOS Debugging: Stack overflow detection, task state visua
---
ssing via task notification and queues.
 RTOS Debugging: Stack overflow detection, task state visualization, and runtime statistics.
Phase 5 — IoT Connectivity
Connecting embedded devices to cloud platforms opens powerful monitoring and control capabilities.
 Wi-Fi: ESP32 with ESP-IDF or Arduino framework for Wi-Fi connected IoT devices.
 MQTT: Lightweight publish-subscribe protocol ideal for IoT sensor data transmission.
 BLE: Bluetooth Low Energy for short-range wireless communication in w
---
oT sensor data transmission.
 BLE: Bluetooth Low Energy for short-range wireless communication in wearables and beacons.
 LoRaWAN: Long-range, low-power wide-area network for agricultural, environmental, and urban IoT.

Phase 6 — Cloud Integration and Edge Computing
Production IoT systems require cloud backends and edge intelligence.
 AWS IoT Core: MQTT broker, device shadows, and IoT rules for routing and processing sensor data.
 Azure IoT Hub: Enterprise-grade device management and telemet
---
routing and processing sensor data.
 Azure IoT Hub: Enterprise-grade device management and telemetry ingestion platform from Microsoft.
 Edge ML: TensorFlow Lite and Edge Impulse for running inference on microcontrollers.
 OTA Updates: Secure over-the-air firmware update systems for deployed device fleets.

Database Engineering Roadmap
 Mastering relational databases, data modeling, and modern data architecture
Introduction
Every application that stores information relies on a database. Database engineers design, implement, optimize,
and maintain the
---
information relies on a database. Database engineers design, implement, optimize,
and maintain the data systems that power software products. This encompasses relational databases, NoSQL
systems, data warehouses, and modern cloud-native data platforms. With data volumes growing exponentially,
the demand for skilled database engineers and architects continues to increase.
This roadmap is suitable for developers looking to deepen their database skills and those targeting dedicated data
engineerin
---
for developers looking to deepen their database skills and those targeting dedicated data
engineering or database administration roles. Professional readiness can be achieved in 8 to 12 months.
Phase 1 — Relational Database Fundamentals
The relational model remains the dominant paradigm for transactional data. Spend 4 to 6 weeks.
 SQL Core: SELECT, INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE, and DDL statements for creating and modifying tables.
 JOINs: INNER, LEFT, RIGHT, FULL OUTER, CROSS, and SELF joins with pr
---
reating and modifying tables.
 JOINs: INNER, LEFT, RIGHT, FULL OUTER, CROSS, and SELF joins with practical query exercises.
 Aggregations: GROUP BY, HAVING, COUNT, SUM, AVG, MIN, MAX, and ROLLUP.
 Subqueries and CTEs: Correlated subqueries, inline views, and Common Table Expressions for readable
complex queries.
Phase 2 — Advanced SQL
Advanced SQL skills separate proficient engineers from basic users. Allow 4 to 5 weeks.
 Window Functions: ROW_NUMBER, RANK, DENSE_RANK, LAG, LEAD, NTILE, and
---
users. Allow 4 to 5 weeks.
 Window Functions: ROW_NUMBER, RANK, DENSE_RANK, LAG, LEAD, NTILE, and running totals with
OVER clauses.
 Indexes: B-tree, hash, GIN, and GiST indexes; composite indexes; covering indexes; and index-only scans.
 Query Optimization: EXPLAIN ANALYZE, execution plans, index selectivity, and identifying slow queries.
 Stored Procedures and Triggers: Business logic encapsulation and automated event-driven data processing.

Phase 3 — Data Modeling
Well-designed schemas
---
sulation and automated event-driven data processing.

Phase 3 — Data Modeling
Well-designed schemas prevent performance issues and data integrity problems. Spend 3 to 4 weeks.
 Normalization: First through Fifth Normal Form — eliminating redundancy and ensuring data integrity.
 ER Diagrams: Entity-Relationship modeling using tools like dbdiagram.io, Lucidchart, or draw.io.
 Dimensional Modeling: Star and snowflake schemas for analytical data warehouses.
 Partitioning: Range, list, and hash p
---
: Star and snowflake schemas for analytical data warehouses.
 Partitioning: Range, list, and hash partitioning for managing large tables efficiently.
Phase 4 — PostgreSQL Deep Dive
PostgreSQL is the most feature-rich open-source relational database in 2026. Spend 4 to 6 weeks.
 JSONB: Storing and querying semi-structured JSON data alongside relational data.
 Full-Text Search: tsvector, tsquery, and GIN indexes for native text search without Elasticsearch.
 Replication: Streaming replication
---
and GIN indexes for native text search without Elasticsearch.
 Replication: Streaming replication for high availability and read scaling with read replicas.
 pg_stat_statements: Query performance monitoring and identifying top resource-consuming queries.
Phase 5 — NoSQL Databases
Different data access patterns require different database paradigms.
 MongoDB: Document model, aggregation pipeline, change streams, and Atlas cloud service.
 Redis: In-memory data structures, pub/sub messaging, so
---
, change streams, and Atlas cloud service.
 Redis: In-memory data structures, pub/sub messaging, sorted sets for leaderboards, and session storage.
 Apache Cassandra: Wide-column store optimized for high-throughput writes and time-series data.
 Choosing the Right Database: CAP theorem, ACID vs BASE, and workload characterization.

Phase 6 — Data Warehousing and Cloud
Modern data platforms separate transactional and analytical workloads.
 Snowflake: Cloud-native data warehouse with automatic
---
ate transactional and analytical workloads.
 Snowflake: Cloud-native data warehouse with automatic scaling and separation of storage and compute.
 BigQuery: Serverless analytics engine from Google optimized for large-scale SQL queries.
 dbt: Data transformation tool for building tested, version-controlled analytical pipelines.
 Apache Iceberg: Open table format for managing petabyte-scale analytical datasets across cloud storage.

AI and Prompt Engineering Roadmap

Introduction
Prompt engineering has emerged as a distinct professional discipline as large language models (LLMs) become
core infrastructure for software products and business workflows. In 2026, practitioners who can effectively
design, test, and optimize prompts and AI pipelines are in high demand across every sector. This roadmap covers
both the practical craft of pr
---
pipelines are in high demand across every sector. This roadmap covers
both the practical craft of prompt engineering and the broader skill set required for AI product development roles.
This roadmap targets software developers, product managers, researchers, and anyone building AI-powered
applications. Basic familiarity with Python is beneficial for the technical components.
Phase 1 — LLM Fundamentals
Understanding how LLMs work provides the mental model needed for effective prompting. Allow 2 t
---
tals
Understanding how LLMs work provides the mental model needed for effective prompting. Allow 2 to 3 weeks.
 Transformer Architecture: Self-attention, tokenization, context windows, and temperature parameters.
 Training and Fine-tuning: Pretraining, RLHF, instruction tuning, and how training shapes model behavior.
 Major Models: GPT-4o, Claude 3.5 Sonnet, Gemini 1.5 Pro, Llama 3, and their capability profiles.
 Model Limitations: Hallucinations, knowledge cutoffs, reasoning failures, and
---
apability profiles.
 Model Limitations: Hallucinations, knowledge cutoffs, reasoning failures, and consistency issues.
Phase 2 — Core Prompt Engineering Techniques
Master the fundamental techniques that form the basis of all advanced prompt work. Allow 4 to 6 weeks.
 Zero-Shot and Few-Shot Prompting: Providing examples in the prompt to guide output format and style.
 Chain of Thought (CoT): Instructing models to reason step by step before producing final answers.
 Role Prompting: Assigning e
---
tructing models to reason step by step before producing final answers.
 Role Prompting: Assigning expert personas to elicit domain-specific knowledge and tone.
 Structured Output: Prompting for JSON, XML, or Markdown-formatted responses for programmatic parsing.

Phase 3 — Advanced Prompting Strategies
Advanced techniques unlock capabilities beyond basic prompting. Spend 4 to 5 weeks.
 ReAct Framework: Combining reasoning and acting — models plan, use tools, observe results, and iterate.
 Se
---
amework: Combining reasoning and acting — models plan, use tools, observe results, and iterate.
 Self-Consistency: Generating multiple reasoning paths and selecting the most consistent answer.
 Tree of Thoughts: Exploring multiple reasoning branches simultaneously for complex problem solving.
 Prompt Chaining: Breaking complex tasks into sequential prompt chains where each output feeds the next.

Phase 4 — RAG and Knowledge Integration
Retrieval Augmented Generation enables LLMs to access external, up-to-date knowledge bases.
 Vector Databases: Pinecone, Weaviate, Chroma, and pgvector for semantic similarity search.
 Embedding Models: OpenAI text-embedding-3, Cohere embed, and open-source models for text
vectorization.
 Chunking Strategies: Fixed-size, semantic, and hierarchical chunking for effective document retrieval.
 RAG Evaluation: RAGAS framework for measuring context releva
---
ing for effective document retrieval.
 RAG Evaluation: RAGAS framework for measuring context relevance, faithfulness, and answer quality.
Phase 5 — AI Agents and Orchestration
Autonomous AI agents represent the frontier of applied LLM engineering in 2026.
 Agent Frameworks: LangChain, LlamaIndex, and CrewAI for building multi-step AI workflows.
 Tool Use and Function Calling: Enabling LLMs to call APIs, query databases, and execute code.
 Multi-Agent Systems: Designing collaborative agent ne
---
all APIs, query databases, and execute code.
 Multi-Agent Systems: Designing collaborative agent networks with specialized roles and handoffs.
 Agent Evaluation: Measuring task completion rates, cost efficiency, and failure mode analysis.

Phase 6 — AI Product Development
Building reliable AI products requires engineering discipline beyond prompt design.
 Prompt Management: PromptLayer, Langsmith, and Helicone for prompt versioning and performance
tracking.
 Evaluation Pipelines: Building au
---
th, and Helicone for prompt versioning and performance
tracking.
 Evaluation Pipelines: Building automated evaluation suites with ground truth datasets and LLM-as-judge.
 Cost Optimization: Token counting, model selection trade-offs, caching with semantic similarity, and batching.
 Safety and Alignment: Guardrails, content filtering, jailbreak resistance, and responsible AI practices.

Introduction
Flutter is Google open-source UI framework that enables developers to build natively compiled applications for
mobile, web, and desktop from a single Dart codebase. In 2026, Flutter has matured into a production-grade
framework adopted by thousands of companies globally including major enterprises and fast-growing startups. Its
expressive widget system and high performance make it one of the most compelling cross-platform choices
a
---
ssive widget system and high performance make it one of the most compelling cross-platform choices
available.
This roadmap is structured for beginners with general programming familiarity and targets developers who want to
ship polished mobile applications efficiently. Professional readiness is achievable in 8 to 12 months.
Phase 1 — Dart Programming Language
Dart is Flutter native language. Spend 2 to 3 weeks achieving Dart proficiency before touching Flutter.
 Dart Basics: Variables, types, n
---
2 to 3 weeks achieving Dart proficiency before touching Flutter.
 Dart Basics: Variables, types, null safety, functions, classes, mixins, and extension methods.
 Asynchronous Dart: Future, async/await, Stream, and isolates for concurrent programming.
 Null Safety: Understanding nullable and non-nullable types — a foundational Dart 2.12 feature.
 Collections: List, Map, Set, and functional collection methods (map, where, fold, reduce).
Phase 2 — Flutter Fundamentals
Learn the Flutter widget
---

enterprise.

egration

QA and Software Testing Roadmap
 Ensuring software quality through manual testing, automation, and modern QA engineering
Introduction
Quality Assurance engineering ensures that software products meet their functional, performance, and security
requirements before reaching end users. In 2026, QA has evolved significantly from manual click-testing into a
---
s before reaching end users. In 2026, QA has evolved significantly from manual click-testing into a
sophisticated engineering discipline involving test automation frameworks, performance engineering, and
continuous testing pipelines integrated directly into CI/CD workflows. QA engineers are critical contributors to
every product team.
This roadmap guides learners from manual testing fundamentals through professional-level automation
engineering. Those with existing programming experience will pr
---
hrough professional-level automation
engineering. Those with existing programming experience will progress faster through the automation phases.
Phase 1 — Software Testing Fundamentals
Every QA engineer begins with a solid theoretical foundation. Allow 3 to 4 weeks.
 Testing Principles: ISTQB principles — testing shows presence of defects, exhaustive testing is impossible,
early testing saves cost.
 Testing Types: Functional, non-functional, structural, regression, smoke, sanity, and explorato
---
t.
 Testing Types: Functional, non-functional, structural, regression, smoke, sanity, and exploratory testing.
 Test Levels: Unit, integration, system, and acceptance testing in the V-model and Agile contexts.
 Defect Lifecycle: Defect reporting, severity vs priority, status workflow, and bug tracking with Jira.
Phase 2 — Manual Testing Skills
Manual testing remains relevant and is the foundation of all test strategy. Spend 4 to 5 weeks.
 Test Case Design: Equivalence partitioning, boundary
---
on of all test strategy. Spend 4 to 5 weeks.
 Test Case Design: Equivalence partitioning, boundary value analysis, decision tables, and state transition
testing.
 Test Planning: Scope definition, risk-based testing, test estimation, and entry/exit criteria.
 Exploratory Testing: Structured exploration using test charters, session-based testing, and heuristics.
 API Testing: Manual API validation with Postman — testing status codes, response schemas, and edge
cases.

Phase 3 — Test Automation
---
on with Postman — testing status codes, response schemas, and edge

Phase 3 — Test Automation Foundations
Automation is the core skill differentiating junior and senior QA engineers in 2026.
 Programming Language: Python is recommended for QA automation due to simplicity and ecosystem depth.
 Selenium WebDriver: Browser automation fundamentals — element location strategies, waits, and page
object model.
 Playwright: Modern browser automation framework that has largely superseded Seleni
---
e
object model.
 Playwright: Modern browser automation framework that has largely superseded Selenium for new projects.
 pytest: Python testing framework with powerful fixtures, parametrization, and plugin ecosystem.
Phase 4 — API and Service Testing
Backend API testing provides faster, more reliable feedback than UI automation.
 REST API Testing: HTTP methods, authentication schemes, and response validation with pytest and
requests.
 Contract Testing: Pact framework for validating consumer-
---
nse validation with pytest and
requests.
 Contract Testing: Pact framework for validating consumer-provider API contracts in microservice
architectures.
 GraphQL Testing: Query validation, schema testing, and error scenario coverage.
 Database Testing: SQL queries to validate data integrity following business transactions.
Phase 5 — Performance and Security Testing
Non-functional testing is essential for production-ready software quality assurance.
 Load Testing: k6, Locust, or Apache JMeter
---
ential for production-ready software quality assurance.
 Load Testing: k6, Locust, or Apache JMeter for simulating concurrent users and measuring system capacity.
 Performance Metrics: Response time percentiles (P95, P99), throughput, error rates, and resource utilization.
 Security Testing: OWASP ZAP for automated vulnerability scanning, and manual OWASP Top 10 testing.
 Accessibility Testing: Axe DevTools and screen reader testing for WCAG compliance validation.

Phase 6 — CI/CD Integratio
---
: Axe DevTools and screen reader testing for WCAG compliance validation.

Phase 6 — CI/CD Integration and QA Engineering
Modern QA engineers integrate testing directly into development pipelines.
 CI Pipeline Integration: Running test suites automatically in GitHub Actions, Jenkins, or GitLab CI.
 Test Reporting: Allure Report and pytest-html for comprehensive, shareable test execution reports.
 Test Data Management: Factory patterns, fixtures, and database seeding for isolated, repeatable te
---
 Test Data Management: Factory patterns, fixtures, and database seeding for isolated, repeatable tests.
 Shift-Left Testing: Involving QA in requirements review, design critique, and code review processes.

Open Source Contribution Roadmap
 Building reputation, skills, and community impact through open source participation
Introduction
Contributing to open source software is one of the most effective ways to accelerate career growth as a
developer. Open source contributions demonstrate initiative, collaboration skills, and technical ability far more
convincingly than per
---
s demonstrate initiative, collaboration skills, and technical ability far more
convincingly than personal projects alone. In 2026, many top technology companies explicitly evaluate GitHub
profiles and open source work during hiring processes.
This roadmap guides developers from first-time contributors through maintainers and project leaders. It is suitable
for developers at all skill levels — meaningful contributions do not require expert-level programming skill.
Phase 1 — Preparation and Mindse
---
ingful contributions do not require expert-level programming skill.
Phase 1 — Preparation and Mindset
Successful contributors prepare before submitting their first pull request. Allow 2 to 3 weeks.
 Git and GitHub Mastery: Forking, cloning, branching, committing, pushing, and pull request workflow.
 Markdown: Writing clear README files, issue descriptions, and pull request documentation.
 Reading Code: Developing the ability to navigate and understand an unfamiliar codebase efficiently.
 Com
---
ng Code: Developing the ability to navigate and understand an unfamiliar codebase efficiently.
 Community Norms: Codes of conduct, contributor guidelines, and professional communication standards.
Phase 2 — Finding the Right Project
Choosing an appropriate first project dramatically affects the contribution experience.

 Projects You Already Use: Contributing to tools you depend on
---
d" labels in your technology stack.
 Projects You Already Use: Contributing to tools you depend on provides natural motivation and context.
 Community Health: Review contributor activity, response times, and tone in past issues before committing.
 Platforms: GitHub Explore, Up for Grabs, First Timers Only, and CodeTriage for curated beginner issues.

Phase 3 — Making Your First Contributions
Start small, be thorough, and build credibility through quality before quantity.
 Documentation: Fixi
---
art small, be thorough, and build credibility through quality before quantity.
 Documentation: Fixing typos, improving examples, and clarifying confusing sections are high-value first
contributions.
 Bug Fixes: Reproduce reported bugs locally, understand root causes, and submit targeted minimal fixes.
 Test Coverage: Adding unit or integration tests for untested code paths.
 Issue Triage: Reproducing unverified issues, adding labels, and requesting additional information.
Phase 4 — Advancing
---
oducing unverified issues, adding labels, and requesting additional information.
Phase 4 — Advancing to Meaningful Features
After establishing trust with maintainers, tackle more impactful contribution types.
 Feature Proposals: Open a GitHub Discussion or issue to propose and align on features before
implementation.
 Refactoring: Improving code quality, performance, or architecture in areas you understand deeply.
 Internationalization: Adding translations for applications with i18n support.
---
understand deeply.
 Internationalization: Adding translations for applications with i18n support.
 Performance Improvements: Profiling, identifying bottlenecks, and submitting benchmarked optimizations.
Phase 5 — Becoming a Trusted Contributor
Regular, high-quality contributions lead to expanded responsibilities and recognition.
 Code Review Participation: Review other contributors pull requests with constructive, encouraging feedback.
 Mentoring: Help first-time contributors navigate the c
---
ts with constructive, encouraging feedback.
 Mentoring: Help first-time contributors navigate the codebase and contribution process.
 Release Process: Understanding changelogs, semantic versioning, and release note preparation.
 Community Building: Answering questions in Discord, Slack, or GitHub Discussions to strengthen community.

Trusted contributors may be invited to become project maintainers or start their own projects.

through documentation and community engagement.

Native vs Cross-Platform Development
 Native Apps: Developed specifically for one platform (Android or iOS). Favored by major
tech companies, high industry demand.
 Cross-Platform Apps: Single codebase runs on both Android and iOS. Saves time and effort.

---
fort.

 Android development: Minimum 8GB RAM, preferably 16GB. Uses heavy IDEs like Android
Studio.
 iOS development: Requires a strong system and macOS.
 Cross-platform development: No OS constraints, more hardware flexibility.

DevOps Engineer Roadmap 2025
1. Role Overview
DevOps bridges Development (build, code, test) and Operations (deploy, maintain). The DevOps engineer ensures
seamless, automated, continuous deployment of application updates without manual intervention.
Entry point: Most DevOps engineers start as software developers, software engineers, or database administrators
before transitioning.

---
: Argo CD, Flux
Learning Order Summary
1. Command line, networking, scripting, Git
2. Cloud fundamentals (AWS)
3. Docker and containerization
4. CI/CD pipeline automation
5. Terraform and Ansible (IaC)
6. Kubernetes orchestration
7. Prometheus and Grafana (monitoring)
8. Service Mesh and GitOps (optional advanced)
Approach: Master one tool at a time before moving to the next.


🎮 GAME DEVELOPMENT ROADMAP 
📌 Overview 
This roadmap guides learners from beginner to advanced levels in game developme
---
ROADMAP 
📌 Overview 
This roadmap guides learners from beginner to advanced levels in game development, 
covering programming, tools, design, and publishing. 
 
🧩 1. Foundations 
Programming 
Choose one language: 
• C# (Unity) 
• C++ (Unreal Engine) 
• Python (Basics) 
Core Concepts 
• Variables, loops, functions 
• Object-Oriented Programming (OOP) 
• Data structures 
Math Basics 
• Vectors (movement, direction) 
• Coordinate systems (2D/3D) 
• Basic physics 
 
🕹️ 2. Game Engine Selection 
Choo
---
ment, direction) 
• Coordinate systems (2D/3D) 
• Basic physics 
 
🕹️ 2. Game Engine Selection 
Choose one engine: 
• Unity → Beginner-friendly, C#, 2D & 3D 
• Unreal Engine → High-end graphics, C++ 
• Godot → Lightweight, beginner-friendly 
 
🎯 3. Build Small Games 
Start with simple projects: 
• Pong 
• Snake 
• Flappy Bird clone 
• Basic platformer 
Key Concepts 
• Game loop 
• Input handling 
• Collision detection 
• UI basics 
 
🎨 4. Game Design Fundamentals 
• Core gameplay mechanics 
• Pl
---
• Collision detection 
• UI basics 
 
🎨 4. Game Design Fundamentals 
• Core gameplay mechanics 
• Player feedback 
• Difficulty balancing 
• Level design 
 
🎧 5. Assets (Art & Audio) 
Tools 
• Aseprite (2D art) 
• Blender (3D modeling) 
• Audacity (audio editing) 
Asset Sources 
• itch.io 
• OpenGameArt 
 
🧠 6. Intermediate Skills 
• Physics systems 
• Animation 
• AI (NPC behavior, pathfinding) 
• Save/load systems 
• Basic shaders 
Version Control 
• Git 
• GitHub 
 
🌐 7. Publishing 
Platforms
---
• Save/load systems 
• Basic shaders 
Version Control 
• Git 
• GitHub 
 
🌐 7. Publishing 
Platforms: 
• Steam 
• itch.io 
• Google Play Store 
 
🚀 8. Advanced Topics 
• Multiplayer networking 
• Procedural generation 
• Advanced graphics & shaders 
• Optimization techniques 
• Monetization strategies 
 
👥 9. Portfolio Development 
Include: 
• 3–5 polished games 
• Gameplay videos 
• Source code 
• Playable builds 
 
⏱️ Suggested Timeline 
Phase Duration 
Foundations 1–2 
months

⚠️ Common Mistakes 
• Starting large projects too early 
• Switching tools frequently 
• Not finishing projects 
• Ignoring polish 
 
💡 Key Insight 
Focus on completing small projects consistently. Iteration builds mastery faster than 
perfection.

AI ENGINEER ROADMAP
Introduction:
An AI Engineer builds intelligent systems using machine learning, deep learning, and data
processing.
Beginner Level:
- Learn Python programming
- Understand basic
---
, deep learning, and data
processing.
Beginner Level:
- Learn Python programming
- Understand basic mathematics (Linear Algebra, Probability, Statistics)
- Learn data handling using NumPy and Pandas
- Basics of machine learning concepts
Intermediate Level:
- Study machine learning algorithms (Regression, Classification)
- Work with Scikit-learn
- Learn data visualization (Matplotlib, Seaborn)
- Start small ML projects
Advanced Level:
- Learn Deep Learning (Neural Networks, CNN, RNN)
- Use framew
---
art small ML projects
Advanced Level:
- Learn Deep Learning (Neural Networks, CNN, RNN)
- Use frameworks like TensorFlow and PyTorch
- Understand NLP and Computer Vision
- Work on real-world datasets
Projects:
- Build a spam classifier
- Create a recommendation system
- Image classification model
Deployment:
- Learn FastAPI or Flask
- Deploy models using Docker
- Use cloud platforms (AWS, GCP)
WEB DEVELOPMENT ROADMAP

Beginner Level:
- Learn HTML, CSS, JavaScript
- Understand how the web works
I
---

PHASE 1: THE FOUNDATION (BEGINNER A1-A2) 
Timeframe: Months 1 to 3 
Objective: Establishing muscular memory, mastering high-frequency vocabulary, 
and developing basic phonetic awareness. 
The Trap: Spending too much time reading and writing instead of speaking. 
1.1 The Mechanics of Sound (Phonetics)

too much time reading and writing instead of speaking. 
1.1 The Mechanics of Sound (Phonetics) 
Before speaking words, you must master sounds. English has 26 letters but 44 
distinct sounds (phonemes). 
• Vowels and Diphthongs: English is a vowel-heavy language. You must 
distinguish between short and long vowels (e.g., "ship" vs. "sheep", "pull" vs. 
"pool"). 
• Consonant Clusters: Practice linking consonants without inserting extra 
vowels (e.g., "str" in "street", not "istreet"). 
• The Schw
---
ing consonants without inserting extra 
vowels (e.g., "str" in "street", not "istreet"). 
• The Schwa (/ə/): The most common sound in English. It is the lazy, 
unstressed vowel sound found in the second syllable of "wa-ter" or the first 
syllable of "a-bout." Mastering the Schwa is the first step to sounding natural. 
1.2 High-Frequency Vocabulary 
Do not learn random words. The Oxford English Corpus shows that just 100 core 
words make up 50% of all spoken English, and 1,000 words make up 85%.
---
pus shows that just 100 core 
words make up 50% of all spoken English, and 1,000 words make up 85%. 
• Focus Areas: Verbs of being and action (be, have, do, go, say, get, make). 
• Survival Phrases: Memorize full chunks rather than individual words. 
o Instead of learning: "Where," "is," "the," "station." 
o Learn the chunk: "Excuse me, how do I get to..."

The Trap: The "Intermediate Plateau," where learners feel stuck because basic

2.1 Crossing the Translation Barrier 
Beginners think in their native language and translate to English before speaking. 
This causes hesitation. To speak fluently, you must "think" in English. 
• Stop using bilingual dictionaries: Switch exclusively t
---
ak fluently, you must "think" in English. 
• Stop using bilingual dictionaries: Switch exclusively to English-to-English 
dictionaries (like Oxford Learner’s or Cambridge). Learn the concept of a 
word, not its native equivalent. 
• Visual Association: When you see a chair, your brain should fire the word 
"chair," not your native word first. 
2.2 The Physics of Connected Speech 
Native speakers do not say words individually; they chain them together into 
continuous sound waves. 
• Catenation (
---
o not say words individually; they chain them together into 
continuous sound waves. 
• Catenation (Linking): When a word ends in a consonant and the next begins 
with a vowel, they link. ("An apple" becomes "a-napple"). 
• Assimilation: Sounds blend to create new sounds. ("Don't you" sounds like 
"Don-chu"). 
• Elision: Disappearing sounds to save time. ("Camera" is pronounced "Cam-
ra," skipping the middle 'e'). 
• Weak Forms: Small grammar words (to, at, for, and, but) are rarely 
pronounced
---
the middle 'e'). 
• Weak Forms: Small grammar words (to, at, for, and, but) are rarely 
pronounced fully. "I want to go" becomes "I wanna go." 
2.3 Expanding the Arsenal: Phrasal Verbs & Idioms 
Native English relies heavily on phrasal verbs rather than formal Latin-based verbs. 
• Shift your vocabulary: 
o Instead of "tolerate," use "put up with." 
o Instead of "discover," use "find out." 
o Instead of "postpone," use "put off."

3.1 Mastering Prosody: Stress, Rhythm, and Intonation 
Fluency is not just speed; it is rhythm. English is a "stress-timed" language. 
• Word Stress: Emphasizing the correct syllable (e.g., PHO-to-graph vs. pho-
TOG-ra-phy). 
• Sentence Stress: Native speakers only stress the "content words" (Nouns, 
Main Verbs, Adjectives) and rush through "structure words" (articles, 
pr
---
e "content words" (Nouns, 
Main Verbs, Adjectives) and rush through "structure words" (articles, 
prepositions). 
• Intonation: * Falling intonation for statements and wh-questions (Who, What, 
Where). 
o Rising intonation for Yes/No questions. 
o Flat or mixed intonation to convey sarcasm, doubt, or nuance. 
3.2 Complex Output & Discourse Markers 
You must transition from simple SVO (Subject-Verb-Object) sentences to complex, 
multi-clause arguments. 
• Discourse Markers: These are the "glue" t
---

multi-clause arguments. 
• Discourse Markers: These are the "glue" that holds fluent speech together 
and gives your brain a microsecond to think. 
o Examples: "As a matter of fact," "To be honest," "At the end of the 
day," "Moving on to..." 
• Spoken Conditionals: Master "If" statements in real-time. ("If I had known, I 
wouldn't have gone.") 
• Hedging: The art of softening statements, crucial for polite, advanced 
communication. ("It seems to me that this migh
---
f softening statements, crucial for polite, advanced

issue.") 
3.3 Active Correction Strategy 
• Record yourself speaking for 5 minutes. 
• Listen back and transcribe exactly what you said, including the "umms" and 
errors. 
• Rewrite the transcription into perfect, advanced English. 
• Speak the corrected version aloud.

PHASE 4: PROFESSIONAL & EXECUTIVE MASTERY 
(C2 & BUSINESS ENGLISH) 
Timeframe: Months 19 to 24+ 
Objective: Commanding authority, mastering industry-specific lexicon, public 
speaking, and navigating cultural pragmatics. 
The Trap: Sounding too informal in boardrooms or too robotic/academic in casual 
networking.

Professional English requires high diplomatic intelligence. You must balance clarity

4.2 The STAR Method for Interviews and Presentations 
When speaking professionally, structure is as important as vocabulary. Train yourself 
to answer complex questions using the STAR framework: 
• S - Situation: Set the context quickly. 
• T - Task: What was the specific problem or goal? 
• A - Action: What did you explicitly do to solve it? 
• R - Result: What was th
---
c problem or goal? 
• A - Action: What did you explicitly do to solve it? 
• R - Result: What was the quantifiable outcome? 
4.3 Industry-Specific Lexicon 
At this stage, general vocabulary is insufficient. You must build a micro-vocabulary 
specific to your domain (Tech, Finance, Medicine, Law). 
• Collocations: Words that naturally go together. (e.g., You "mitigate risk," you 
do not "decrease risk." You "leverage assets," you "drive consensus.")

THE PSYCHOLOGICAL ROADMAP: OVERCOMING 
THE "AFFECTIVE FILTER" 
The greatest barrier to spoken English is not intellectual; it is emotional. Linguist 
Stephen Krashen defines the "Affective Filter" as the psychological block caused by 
anxiety, fear of failure, or lack of motivation. 
1. Embrace the "Idiot" Phase: You will sound less intelligent in English than 
y
---
ack of motivation. 
1. Embrace the "Idiot" Phase: You will sound less intelligent in English than 
you do in your native language for the first year. Accept this. Ego is the enemy 
of fluency. 
2. Accuracy vs. Fluency: In Phase 1 and 2, prioritize Fluency (the ability to 
keep talking without stopping). In Phase 3 and 4, shift your focus to Accuracy 
(fixing grammatical errors). If you focus on accuracy too early, you will 
develop a stutter and severe speaking anxiety. 
3. The "Good Enough" Pri
---
curacy too early, you will 
develop a stutter and severe speaking anxiety. 
3. The "Good Enough" Principle: The goal of spoken language is the transfer 
of information. If the listener understood your point, the communication was 
100% successful, even if you used the wrong verb tense. 
 

THE DATA ENGINE: ARCHITECTING

SECTION 1: THE INGESTION LAYER (DATA SOURCES) 
1.1 Common Crawl: The Digital Library of Babel 
Common Crawl provides a massive, open-source repositor
---
1 Common Crawl: The Digital Library of Babel 
Common Crawl provides a massive, open-source repository of web crawl data. For a 
"Pro" engineer, handling this isn't about downloading files; it's about navigating WARC 
(Web ARChive) files. 
1. WARC Files: The standard format for storing web crawls. It includes the raw 
HTTP response, headers, and metadata. 
2. WET Files: Extracted plain text from WARC files. Using WET files saves petabytes 
of bandwidth during the initial filtering stage. 
3. Samp
---
RC files. Using WET files saves petabytes 
of bandwidth during the initial filtering stage. 
3. Sampling Strategy: You cannot train on all of Common Crawl. Pro-level 
engineering involves "Quality Sampling"—taking snippets from different domains 
to calculate a "Domain Quality Score" before full ingestion. 
1.2 Wikipedia & Curated Knowledge 
Wikipedia is the "Golden Standard" for factual density. 
• Data Dumps: Instead of scraping the live site, engineers use Wikimedia Dumps 
(XML/SQL). 
• Struc
---
• Data Dumps: Instead of scraping the live site, engineers use Wikimedia Dumps 
(XML/SQL). 
• Structural Parsing: Converting MediaWiki markup into clean Markdown or 
JSON. 
• The "Anchor Text" Value: Extracting internal links to build a knowledge graph of 
how concepts relate (e.g., "Python" links to "Programming Language"). 
1.3 Custom Domain Data (The Competitive Edge) 
• ArXiv & Research Papers: Handling LaTeX and PDF parsing (the "Boss Level" of 
data cleaning). 
• GitHub/StackOverflow: Cod
---
s: Handling LaTeX and PDF parsing (the "Boss Level" of 
data cleaning). 
• GitHub/StackOverflow: Code-specific data. Requires removing "Boilerplate" 
and "Dead Code" to ensure the LLM learns logic, not just syntax. 
• Legal/Medical Archives: High-stakes data that requires specific de-
identification to comply with privacy laws (GDPR/HIPAA).

Raw web data is $90\%$ noise (Ads, Navbars, Footers, SEO spam). 
• Tools: trafilatura or BeautifulSoup.

2.2 Language Identification (LangID) 
Training a model on a mix of languages without control leads to "mushy" logic. 
• FastText: The industry standard for identifying 170+ languages in milliseconds. 
• Confidence Thresholding: If a document is only $60\%$ English, it is often 
discarded to prevent "code-switching" noise in the training set. 
 
SECTION 3: PIPELINE STAGE 2 – DEDUPLICATION (THE QUALITY MULTIPLIER) 
Deduplication is the most critical step. Re
---
PELINE STAGE 2 – DEDUPLICATION (THE QUALITY MULTIPLIER) 
Deduplication is the most critical step. Repeated data (duplicates) causes LLMs to 
"memorize" rather than "reason. " 
3.1 Exact Match Deduplication 
Using SHA-256 Hashes to find identical files. This is simple but only catches about 
$5\%$ of duplicates. 
3.2 Fuzzy Deduplication (MinHash / LSH) 
This is where Apache Spark becomes mandatory. 
• Shingling: Breaking text into $n$-grams (sequences of words). 
• MinHash: Creating a small "sign
---
• Shingling: Breaking text into $n$-grams (sequences of words). 
• MinHash: Creating a small "signature" for each document based on its shingles. 
• Locality Sensitive Hashing (LSH): Grouping similar signatures into "buckets. " If 
two documents end up in the same bucket, they are likely duplicates. 
• Jaccard Similarity: Calculating the percentage of shared content. Usually, 
anything above $0.80$ similarity is purged.

SECTION 4: PIPELINE STAGE 3 – HEURISTIC & MODEL-BASED FILTERING 
4.1 Heuristic Filters (The "Gopher" Rules) 
Inspired by DeepMind’s Gopher paper, these are hardcoded rules: 
• Stop-word Ratio: If a text has no "the, " "is, " or "and, " it’s likely gibberish or code, 
not natural language. 
• Symbol-to-Word Ratio: Too many ... or ### indicates SEO spam or a broken 
crawl. 
• Mean Word Length: Human language typically averages 3–7 characters per 
word. Outliers are dis
---
l. 
• Mean Word Length: Human language typically averages 3–7 characters per 
word. Outliers are discarded. 
4.2 Toxicity & PII Scrubbing 
• PII (Personally Identifiable Information): Using Presidio or Regex to redact 
emails, phone numbers, and addresses. 
• Toxicity Classification: Using a small BERT-style model to score text for hate 
speech or adult content.

SECTION 6: EVALUATION METRICS (THE PRO'S SCORECARD) 
6.1 Perplexity ($PP$ or $PPL$) 
Perplexity measures how well a probability model predicts a sample. 
$$PP(W) = P(w_1, w_2, ..., w_N)^{-\frac{1}{N}}$$ 
• Low Perplexity: The model is "surprised" less by the data, indic
---
w_2, ..., w_N)^{-\frac{1}{N}}$$ 
• Low Perplexity: The model is "surprised" less by the data, indicating better 
learning. 
• High Perplexity: The model is confused, often due to noisy or low-quality 
training data. 
6.2 BLEU & ROUGE 
• BLEU (Bilingual Evaluation Understudy): Measures $n$-gram overlap between 
model output and a reference. Essential for translation and summarization 
tasks. 
• ROUGE (Recall-Oriented Understudy for Gisting Evaluation): Focuses on 
"Recall"—how much of the refere
---
UGE (Recall-Oriented Understudy for Gisting Evaluation): Focuses on 
"Recall"—how much of the reference text was actually captured in the summary.
